тАШрдорд╣реЗ рдиреЛ рдЕрджреНрдп ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рддреНрдпрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕ рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдкрд╛рдЩреНрддреНрджрдореБрд╖рд╕реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореНрдпрддреЗ рдЪ – тАШ рдорд╣реЗ рджрд╢ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╛ рдЙрд╖рд╕реНрдпрдВ рддреБ рдкрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреЗ рдЙрд╖рд╕реНрдпреЗ рдХреНрд░рддреМ рдкрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрддреЗ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗ рдЪреЗрджрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░реНрдпрддреЗ рд╣рд┐ - рдорд╣реЗ рдиреЛ рдЕрджреНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрддрдореН ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рек. резрек ) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

79 (433)
Dawn
Satya┼Ыravas ─Аtreya
10 verses: paс╣Еkti
A hymn with a remarkably unwavering focus on material gain. Since the priestly gifts (dakс╣гiс╣З─Б) are distributed at the dawn ritual, the goddess Dawn is often associated

with wealth and giving, but here very little attention is given to any other aspect of the goddess. The tone is set by the increasingly monotonous refrain: тАЬo well-born lady, liberal with horses.тАЭ Several patrons are named in the first verses (1тАУ3), and the poet hopes that patrons in general will be the recipients of DawnтАЩs bounty, in order for them to redistribute it to the poets (4тАУ8).
The usual attention to DawnтАЩs beauty, her first appearance, her journey, her cows, and so forth is entirely missing in this hymn, which does, however, con tain one striking image, in verse 9. Why a laggard Dawn would be compared to a thief isnтАЩt entirely clear, but it is quite possibly because thieves worked at night.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Dawn The meter of this hymn is Paс╣Еkti, with five 8-syllable p─Бdas. The fifth in all vss. is the refrain, a voc. phrase s├║j─Бte a┼Ыvas┼лnс╣Ыte тАЬo well-born lady, liberal with horses,тАЭ which is essentially detachable. So the hymn comes across as standard Anuс╣гс╣нubh, with an appended and superfluous refrain. As indicated in the published translation, the contents are for the most part uninspired, contrary to most Dawn hymns, though closer inspection reveals more intricate patterns than a superficial reading turned up.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRadiant Uс╣гas, wake up today for (the acquisition of) ample riches, in like manner as you have awakened us (of old); bright-born, and praised sincerely for (the gift of) horses, show favour to satya┼Ыravas, the son of Vayya.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The concluding phrase is the refrain of the following verses: suj─Бte a┼Ыvas┼лnс╣Ыte: suj─Бt─Б, well-born = ┼Ыobhanapr─Бdur bh┼лta, becoming manifest with splendour or light; a┼Ыvasunс╣Ыta, she whose praise for the sake of horses is affectionate and true, svartha priyasaty─Бtmika stutiv─Бk yasy─Бс╕е sa

Jamison Brereton

Awaken us today for great wealth, o Dawn, as heaven-bright one,
just as you also awakened us at Satya┼Ыravas V─БyyaтАЩs
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase mah├й тАж r─Бy├й div├нtmat─л is very reminiscent of IV.31.11 mah├│ r─Бy├й div├нtmate, with an adverbial mah├бс╕е but a dat. div├нtmate modifying r─Бy├й. See comm. ad loc. It seems likely that our fem. div├нtmat─л is a nonce adaptation to the fem.

context. As for div├нtmant-, I now tentatively accept the analysis of div├нt- as containing the root noun -i-t- and would alter the tr. to тАЬas one coming from heavenтАЭ or тАЬas heaven-sent one.тАЭ

01-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These three vss. follow the same pattern: Dawn is urged to repeat for us now a previous action she performed in the presence of and for the benefit of a previous patron. The name Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya appears in all three vss. (The Anukr.

attributes the hymn to Satya┼Ыravas ─Аtreya, but as Geldner points out [n. 1d] he is surely the patron, not the poet.) Curiously in vss. 1 and 3 Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya is identified as the previous patron, while in vs. 2 he is the current patron and the previous patron has a different name. This chronological slippage is somewhat confusing – and is emphasized by having identical clauses differing only in the tense/mood of the verb and the demonstrative vs. relative pronoun: 2cd s─Б╠Бvy ├╣cha s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й 3cd y├│ vya├║chaс╕е s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й The insistence on this generous patron of the past has a purpose: there is a parallel insistence on the patrons of today in the rest of the hymn. Although only Dawn is addressed, the poet is clearly sending a message to the patrons, to generously redistribute the wealth that Dawn will bestow on them, on the model of Satya┼Ыravas.

Griffith

O HEAVENLY Dawn, awaken us to ample opulence to-day
Even as thou hast wakened us with Satyasravas, Vayya’s son, high-born! delightful with thy steeds!

Geldner

Weck uns heute, o Usas, zu gro├Яem Reichtum, du die Glanzreiche, wie du uns sonst bei Satyasravas Vayya geweckt hast, du Edelgeborene, Ro├Яeschenkende.

Grassmann

Zu grossem Reichthum weck uns heut, o Morgenroth, zu gl├дnzendem; Wie du uns immer aufgeweckt, bei Vajja’s Sohn, Satja├зravas, o edle, rossereiche du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDaughter of heaven, who have dawned upon Sunitha, the son of ┼Ъucadratha, bright-born, and praised sincerely for (the gift of) horses, dawn upon the powerful son of Vayya, Satya┼Ыravas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You who dawned forth at Sun─лtha ┼ЪaucadrathaтАЩs, o Daughter of Heaven, dawn forth at the mightier Satya┼Ыravas V─БyyaтАЩs
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
01-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These three vss. follow the same pattern: Dawn is urged to repeat for us now a previous action she performed in the presence of and for the benefit of a previous patron. The name Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya appears in all three vss. (The Anukr.

attributes the hymn to Satya┼Ыravas ─Аtreya, but as Geldner points out [n. 1d] he is surely the patron, not the poet.) Curiously in vss. 1 and 3 Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya is identified as the previous patron, while in vs. 2 he is the current patron and the previous patron has a different name. This chronological slippage is somewhat confusing – and is emphasized by having identical clauses differing only in the tense/mood of the verb and the demonstrative vs. relative pronoun: 2cd s─Б╠Бvy ├╣cha s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й 3cd y├│ vya├║chaс╕е s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й The insistence on this generous patron of the past has a purpose: there is a parallel insistence on the patrons of today in the rest of the hymn. Although only Dawn is addressed, the poet is clearly sending a message to the patrons, to generously redistribute the wealth that Dawn will bestow on them, on the model of Satya┼Ыravas.

02-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Is the comparative тАШmightierтАЩ (s├бh─лyas-) used to assert that Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya is mightier than Sun─лtha ┼Ъaucadratha? The Pp. reads accented v├н even directly before accented a├║chaс╕е (2b, 3c), where we might expect univerbation and loss of accent on the preverb. The Saс╣Гhit─Б text is of course ambiguous.

s─Б╠Бwith the 2nd ps. impv. ucha simply shows the common use of the s├б/t├бm prn.

with 2nd ps. impvs.; see my 1992 тАЬVedic тАШs├б fig├йтАЩ: An inherited sentence connective?тАЭ Elaborate semantic/functional interpr., like RenouтАЩs тАЬde la m├кme mani├иre, dans les m├кmes conditions (heureuses)тАЭ (EVP 3, ad loc.) or Witzel Got┼НтАЩs y─Б╠БтАж s─Б╠БтАж тАЬwelche du тАж als solche duтАЭ are unnec.

Daughter of Heaven, thou dawnedst on Sunitha Sucadratha’s son,
So dawn thou on one mightier still, on Satyasravas, Vayya’s son, high-born! delightful with thy steeds!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDaughter of heaven, who are the bringer of opulence, dawn upon us today, as, bright-born, and praised for (the gift of) horses, you have dawned upon the powerful Satya┼Ыravas, the son of Vayya.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As one bringing goods hither, dawn forth for us today, o Daughter of HeavenтАФ
you who dawned forth at the mightier Satya┼Ыravas V─БyyaтАЩs
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

y├│ beginning p─Бda c represents y─Б╠Б+ u (note Pp. y├│ ├нti), but the apparent masc.

form causes a momentary stir.

01-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These three vss. follow the same pattern: Dawn is urged to repeat for us now a previous action she performed in the presence of and for the benefit of a previous patron. The name Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya appears in all three vss. (The Anukr.

attributes the hymn to Satya┼Ыravas ─Аtreya, but as Geldner points out [n. 1d] he is surely the patron, not the poet.) Curiously in vss. 1 and 3 Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya is identified as the previous patron, while in vs. 2 he is the current patron and the previous patron has a different name. This chronological slippage is somewhat confusing – and is emphasized by having identical clauses differing only in the tense/mood of the verb and the demonstrative vs. relative pronoun: 2cd s─Б╠Бvy ├╣cha s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й 3cd y├│ vya├║chaс╕е s├бh─лyasi, satya┼Ыravasi v─Бyy├й The insistence on this generous patron of the past has a purpose: there is a parallel insistence on the patrons of today in the rest of the hymn. Although only Dawn is addressed, the poet is clearly sending a message to the patrons, to generously redistribute the wealth that Dawn will bestow on them, on the model of Satya┼Ыravas.

Is the comparative тАШmightierтАЩ (s├бh─лyas-) used to assert that Satya┼Ыravas V─Бyya is mightier than Sun─лtha ┼Ъaucadratha? The Pp. reads accented v├н even directly before accented a├║chaс╕е (2b, 3c), where we might expect univerbation and loss of accent on the preverb. The Saс╣Гhit─Б text is of course ambiguous.

s─Б╠Бwith the 2nd ps. impv. ucha simply shows the common use of the s├б/t├бm prn.

with 2nd ps. impvs.; see my 1992 тАЬVedic тАШs├б fig├йтАЩ: An inherited sentence connective?тАЭ Elaborate semantic/functional interpr., like RenouтАЩs тАЬde la m├кme mani├иre, dans les m├кmes conditions (heureuses)тАЭ (EVP 3, ad loc.) or Witzel Got┼НтАЩs y─Б╠БтАж s─Б╠БтАж тАЬwelche du тАж als solche duтАЭ are unnec.

рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рд░рд┐ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЛрдкреЗрддреЗ рее рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН тАШ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрд╡рдирд┐рдкреМ’ . рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдирд┐рдкреН ред рднрд╛рддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрддрд░рд┐ рд╡рдирд┐рдкреН рее рдЙрд╖рдГ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрднрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдпреЗ рд╡рд╣реНрдирдпрдГ рд╡реЛрдврд╛рд░рдГ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореИрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реИрдГ рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдордШреИрдГ рд╣реЗ рдордШреЛрдирд┐ рдзрдиреИрд░реНрдзрдирд╡рддрд┐ рддреНрд╡рджрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рддреН рд╕реБрд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареНрд╡рд░реНрдерд┐рднрд┐рд░рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрдгреАрдпрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рджрд╛рдордиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рджрд╛рдирд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реБрд░рд╛рддрдпрдГ ред рд░рд╛рддрд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реБрджрд╛рдирд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe offerers of oblations who eulogize you, lustrous Uс╣гas, with sacred hymns, become prosperous with affluence, (through your favour), bestower of wealth, bright-born goddess, (who are) sincrely praised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The (oblation-)conveyors who greet you with praises, far-radiant oneтАФ those very splendid ones (will become) possessed of gifts and lovely presents, through your bounties, o bounteous one
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With the standard tr. I take cd as the main cl. corresponding to the rel. cl. in ab, despite the lack of a resumptive pronoun and of a verb. The pattern established in the first 3 vss. of alternating rel. and main clauses makes this interpr. likely, even though the subjects have changed.

Contra Geldner, who takes ab as referring to the singers and cd to the patrons, I think both hemistichs refer to the singers. So also Renou and Witzel Got┼Н, an interpr. that goes back to S─Бyaс╣Зa. (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 4). Here the circulation of wealth appears to be a two-way transaction: the poets praise Dawn and receive bounties. How that happens is laid out in the next few vss., which complicate the two-way model.

Griffith

Here round about thee are the priests who laud thee, Bright One, with their hymns,
And men with gifts, O Bounteous Dame, splendid with wealth and offering much, high-born! delightful with thy steeds!

Geldner

Die Opferleiter, die dich mit Lobliedern begr├╝├Яen, du Erstrahlende, diese sollen mit ihren Gaben, du Gabenreiche, die gl├╝ckgesegneten, reichbelohnenden Schenker beschenken, du Edelgeborene, Rosseschenkende.

Grassmann

Die Priester, die, o gl├дnzende, mit Lobges├дngen dich erh├╢hn, Die sei’n, o reiche, hochbegl├╝ckt, an Gaben und an Spenden reich, o edle, rossereiche du.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЙрд╖рдГ рдпрдЪреНрдЪрд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ ред рд╣реАрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рдпрддреН рдпреЗ рдХреЗрдЪрди рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдЗрдореЗ рдкреБрд░рддреЛ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛: рдЧрдгрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдШрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдордШрддреНрддрдпреЗ рдзрдирджрд╛рддрдпреЗ рдзрдирджрд╛рдирд╛рдп рдзрдирд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдп рд╡рд╛ рдЫрджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЙрдкрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╜рдкреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкрд░рд┐ рджрдзреБрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рддреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╖реНрдЯрдпрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреЗрд╡ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЕрд╣реНрд░рдпрдореН рдЕрд╣реНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрдордХреНрд╖реАрдгрдорд▓рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╣рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рдзрдГ рдзрдирдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рджрджрддрдГ рдпрдЬрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрд░реНрдерд┐рднреНрдпреЛрд╜рдХреНрд╖реАрдгрдВ рджрджрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдпреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрджрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╜рдкреНрдпрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердореЗрд╡ рдлрд▓рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдпрдЪреНрдЪрд┐рджреНрдзреАрддреНрдпрддреНрд░ рдпрджреНрдпрдкреАрддрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдпрдореН ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпреЗ рддрдерд╛рдкреАрддреНрдпрдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрд╡рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдореН рее рее реирез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese, your assembled (worshippers), who stand before you to distribute wealth, entertain towards us kindly intentions, offering unlimited riches; bright-born goddess, (who are) sincerely praised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

These your assembled worshippers: yaccid hi te gaс╣З─Б ime chadayanti maghattaye paricid vaс╣гс╣нayo dadhur dadato r─Бdho ahrayam: maghattaye = dhanad─Бn─Бya or dhanavattv─Бya, for giving or for possessing wealth; pari cid va┼Ыtayo dadhuс╕е = asm─Бn eva k─Бmayam─Бnaс╕е parito dh─Бrayanti, desirous of or being kind to us, they support us every way; dadato r─Бdho ahrayam = giving wealth that is not to be wasted or taken away, or of which there is no need to be ashed; i.e. all they who, offering oblations, worship the dawn receive the reward for the benefit of us, or of me, that is, of the author of the hymn, ye tvam havir dadataс╕е stuvanti te sarve apy asmadartham phalam dh─Бrayanti

Jamison Brereton

For whenever these throngs appear to you (fit) for the giving of bounties, eager, they surround those who give immoderate benefit [=patrons]
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two-party sketch in vs. 4 gives way to a three-party model: when Dawn gives them the go-ahead, as it were, the patrons, who have not yet been mentioned in the hymn as a class, bestow bounties on the poets.

This vs. presents some difficulties, not least the referent(s) of the various plurals and their grammatical identity. With most, I take the gaс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е to be the priest/poets who were also the subj. of the preceding vs. and who greeted Dawn with praise in 4ab. The first hemistich of this vs. expresses the potential reciprocity for this praise: Dawn considers its producers worthy to be given bounties, the same bounties referred to in 5c.

I part company with the standard tr. in the 2nd hemistich. Most take the subj.

here to be the patrons, who either physically surround the priest/poets (so I read Oldenberg) while giving to them or have succeeded (using a sense of p├бri тИЪdh─Б [тАШconcludeтАЩ not found till later]) in giving, finished giving to them (Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н). By contrast I consider the subject still to be the priest/poets. They surround the patrons, who are giving to them. d├бdataс╕е is of course grammatically ambiguous: I take it as acc. pl., while the rest interpr. it as nom. pl. The use of the word gaс╣З├б- тАШthrongтАЩ to refer to the poets in ab helps explain the surprisingly physical verb тАШsurroundтАЩ in cd: the picture is of the over-eager (v├бс╣гс╣нi-) ritual recipients almost ganging up on the patrons.

English translation:

тАЬAffluent Uс╣гas, bestow upon these (yor) devout adorers food and posterity, so that, being opulent, they may, without stint, bestow riches upon us; bright-born goddess who are sincerely praised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Upon them confer glory in heroes, bounteous DawnтАФupon the patrons, who, bounteous (themselves), have granted us immoderate benefits
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the patrons, who have properly compensated the priest/poets, receive their own reward from Dawn. Interestingly it is not material, but rather y├б┼Ыas- тАШgloryтАЩ

– though glory consisting of heroes (v─лr├бvat), meaning, narrowly, sons, but also men belonging to our side who will perform well in warfare and acquire battle glory. The emphasis on non-material rewards for the patrons continues in vs. 7 with тАЬlofty brilliance and gloryтАЭ (dyumna╠Рbс╣Ыh├бd y├б┼Ыaс╕е), while the poets receive material gifts, r─Б╠Бdh─Бс╣Гsi ├б┼Ыvy─Б gavy─Б╠БтАЬbenefits consisting of horses and cows.тАЭ For a similar split between material rewards for the singers and non-material ones for the patrons see V.86.6, where the patrons get тАЬlofty fameтАЭ (┼Ыr├бvo bс╣Ыh├бt) and the singers get wealth and refreshment (ray├нm тАж ├нс╣гam).

Griffith

Give to these wealthy patrons fame, O affluent Dawn, with hero sons,
To these our princes who have brought rich gifts ne’er to be reft away, highborn! delightful with thy steeds!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAffluent Uс╣гas, bring wealth and abundant food to those who, liberal givers, bestow upon us riches with horses and cattle; bright-born goddess (who are) sincerely prised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To them bring lofty brilliance and glory, o bounteous Dawn,
to the patrons who apportion to us benefits consisting of horses
and cows
тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
06-07 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the patrons, who have properly compensated the priest/poets, receive their own reward from Dawn. Interestingly it is not material, but rather y├б┼Ыas- тАШgloryтАЩ

– though glory consisting of heroes (v─лr├бvat), meaning, narrowly, sons, but also men belonging to our side who will perform well in warfare and acquire battle glory. The emphasis on non-material rewards for the patrons continues in vs. 7 with тАЬlofty brilliance and gloryтАЭ (dyumna╠Рbс╣Ыh├бd y├б┼Ыaс╕е), while the poets receive material gifts, r─Б╠Бdh─Бс╣Гsi ├б┼Ыvy─Б gavy─Б╠БтАЬbenefits consisting of horses and cows.тАЭ For a similar split between material rewards for the singers and non-material ones for the patrons see V.86.6, where the patrons get тАЬlofty fameтАЭ (┼Ыr├бvo bс╣Ыh├бt) and the singers get wealth and refreshment (ray├нm тАж ├нс╣гam).

Griffith

Bring lofty and resplendent fame, O thou munificent Dawn, to these
Our wealthy patrons who bestow rich gifts on us of steeds and kine, high-born! delightful with thy steeds!

Geldner

Ihnen bring, o gabenreiche Usas, hohen Glanz und Ruhm mit, den freigebigen Herren, die uns Geschenke von Rossen und Rindern zuteilten, du Edelgeborene, Rosseschenkende!

Grassmann

O fahre Sch├дtze, grossen Glanz, o reiche Uschas, diesen zu, Den Opferherren, die mit Ross und Rindern reichlich uns beschenkt, o edle, rossereiche du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDaughter of heaven, Dawn! delay not our (sacred) rite; let not the sun scorch you with his ray, as (a prince punishes) a thief, or (subdues) an enemy; bright-born goddess,(who are), sincerely praised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Dawn forth, Daughter of Heaven. DonтАЩt keep dragging out your work over a long time,
lest the sun scorch you with his beam as (he might) a swindling thief тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The last vs. before the summary vs., this one brings the hymn ringcompositionally back to its beginning with its opening impv. vy ├╣cha тАШdawn forthтАЩ, a lexeme found 4x in vss. 2-3 (2b, 2c, 3b, 3c).

As noted in the published introduction, this prohibition and its striking simile are the most notable features of this hymn. The m─Б╠Бclause contains a present injunctive, not an aorist. Hoffmann (79) explains it as an inhibitive, not a prohibitive – his standard explanation for the use of present injunctives in such contexts. Although Ian Hollenbaugh has demonstrated that this explanation of the use of pres. injunctives with m─Б╠БdoesnтАЩt hold – they are generally used when an aor. injunc. is not available – in this case, HoffmannтАЩs analysis may be correct. There is a perfectly fine root aor. to тИЪtan and it in fact occurs once with m─Б╠Б(I.91.23), so we may need to seek a functional explanation somewhat in the manner of HoffmannтАЩs. On the other hand and after further thought, I wonder if the pres. stem is used in this context in order to express a durative prohibitive, rather than an inhibitive. That is, starting now, when you dawn, donтАЩt dawdle at your work. SheтАЩs just been ordered to dawn, which makes the start time now, not in the past, but the poet fears that once she starts sheтАЩs going to draw it out longer than she should. It shouldnтАЩt be inhibitive in HoffmannтАЩs sense, because that would mean sheтАЩs already started the work. On still another hand, however, since this is functionally the final vs., which refers back to the beginning of the hymn, perhaps the poet is saying that Dawn has been at work since that beginning and should finish it up.

It is difficult not to take s┼л╠Бraс╕е as a nom. sg. to a thematic stem (so, e.g., Geldner and Renou), although many occurrences of s┼л╠Бraс╕е are better interpr. as gen. sg. to sv├аr- – incl. in this same sequence s┼л╠Бro arc├нс╣г─Б in VIII.7.36. Witzel Got┼Н take it as a gen., but then must identify a different subj. for t├бp─Бti, leading them to introduce Varuс╣Зa and a superstructure of explanation that seems over-elaborate. As indicated in the published

introduction, I think the point of contact is the assumption that thieves work at night and if the sun rises on them, they will be caught out.

Griffith

O Daughter of the Sky, shine forth; delay not to perform thy task.
Let not the Sun with fervent heat consume thee like a robber foe, high-born! delightful with the steeds!

Geldner

O Himmelstochter, leuchte auf; und nicht verz├╢gere dein Werk, Damit dich nicht, wie einen Dieb, die Sonne brennt mit ihrem Strahl, o edle, rossereiche du.

English translation:

тАЬYou, Uс╣гas, are able to give (us) whatever, indeed, (has been solicited), and much (that has not been asked for); for, radiant (divinity), who are dawning upon your adorers, you are never cruel (to them);bright-born goddess (who are) sincerely praised for (the gift of) horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

So much you ought to give, o Dawn, or moreтАФ
you who, as you dawn, far-radiant one, do not dwindle for the praisers тАУ o well-born lady, liberal with horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

pram─л╠Бyase is variously rendered, but тАШdiminishтАЩ or the like fits both the root and the context. ThiemeтАЩs principled insistence on тАШtauschen, t├дuschenтАЩ (ZDMG 41 [1941] 107-8 = KlSch 32-33) produces an unconvincing interpr., requiring further shoring up: тАЬтАж die du тАж nicht get├дuscht wirst (= du, deren Absicht zu schenken nicht vereitelt wird).тАЭ That Dawn does not diminish in cd harmonizes with the increase in gifts that the poet urges in ab.

The dat. stotс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е may be construed with uch├бnt─л rather than pram─л╠Бyase, thus тАЬdawning for the praisers, you do not diminishтАЭ (so Renou, Thieme), but this would have no appreciable effect.

Griffith

So much, and more exceedingly, O Dawn, it suits thee to bestow,
Thou Radiant One who ceasest not to shine for those who sing thy praise, highborn! delightful with thy steeds!

So viel oder noch mehr vermagst du, Usas, zu schenken, die du, Erstrahlende, f├╝r die S├дnger nie abnimmst, wenn du aufleuchtest, du Edelgeborene, Rosseschenkende.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реВрдиреГрддреЗ) рдмреЬреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╕реБрдЬрд╛рддреЗ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рд╣реБрдИ (рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рд░рд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рдФрд░ (рдЙрд╖рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░реНрд╡реЗрд▓рд╛ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА ! (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рддреВ (рдПрддрд╛рд╡рддреН) рдЗрддрдиреЗ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд╛) рд╡рд╛ (рднреВрдпрдГ) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд╛) рднреА (рджрд╛рддреБрдореН) рджреЗрдиреЗ рдХреЛ (рдЕрд░реНрд╣рд╕рд┐) рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рдпрд╛) рдЬреЛ рддреВ (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреА) рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реБрдИ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рддреВ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рд╕реЗ (рдЗрддреН) рд╣реА (рди) рдирд╣реАрдВ (рдкреНрд░рдореАрдпрд╕реЗ) рдорд░рддреА рд╣реИ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЙрд╖рд░реНрд╡реЗрд▓рд╛ рдереЛреЬреА рднреА рдмреЬреЗ рдЖрдирдиреНрджреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреЗрддреА рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рддреБрдо рд╣реЛрдУ реерезрежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ рдФрд░ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЙрдирд╛рд╢реАрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмрд╛рдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реВрдиреГрддреЗ рд╕реБрдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рд░реНрдпреБрд╖рд░реНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐ ! рддреНрд╡рдореЗрддрд╛рд╡рджреНрд╡рд╛ рднреВрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рджрд╛рддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рд╕рд┐ рдпрд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдп рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреА рдирд┐рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддреА рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд╕реЗ рд╕рд╛ рддреНрд╡рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреЗрдгреЗрдиреНрди рдкреНрд░рдореАрдпрд╕реЗ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрддрд╛рд╡рддреН) (рд╡рд╛) (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдЙрд╖рдГ) рдЙрд╖рд░реНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рднреВрдпрдГ) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрдореН (рд╡рд╛) рд╡рд╛ (рджрд╛рддреБрдореН) (рдЕрд░реНрд╣рд╕рд┐) (рдпрд╛) (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ (рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рд░рд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдиреЗ (рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреА) рдирд┐рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддреА (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдкреНрд░рдореАрдпрд╕реЗ) рдореНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реЗ (рд╕реБрдЬрд╛рддреЗ) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реВрдиреГрддреЗ) реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛ ! рдпрдереЛрд╖рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкрд╛ рдорд╣рдд рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рднрд╡реЗрддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрд╖рдГрд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЛрдирд╛рд╜рд╢реАрддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬрд╢реА рдЙрд╖рд╛ рдереЛрдбреНрдпрд╛ рд╡реЗрд│рд╛рдд рдкреБрд╖реНрдХрд│ рдЖрдирдВрдж рджреЗрддреЗ рддрд╕реЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд╡реНрд╣рд╛. рее резреж рее
